Special Announcement

Pan Gongzhan's Speech on Shanghai's School Education (V)

When the United States returned the "Boxer Indemnity," educators held a meeting in a certain place. Some people said, "We can use this money to run 'universal education,' and at least a large portion of the money should be used for 'universal education' undertakings." But others said, "This is not allowed. If we use this money for national 'universal education,' this money will not be enough. The funding for 'primary school education' should be provided by each province and county themselves. We don't need to spend the Boxer Indemnity returned by the United States in bits and pieces in each province and county. It is better to use this money to run 'higher education'." Later, as a result of the debate, it was still decided to use this money to run "higher education" and send students to study abroad. The famous "Tsinghua University" was built with this money, and several other universities were also subsidized. Therefore, the "Sino-French," "Sino-Belgian," and "Sino-British" Boxer Indemnities were subsequently used for "higher education." I remember a few days ago a newspaper criticized students studying abroad, and it was said very well: "We spend a lot of money on students studying abroad. The money is no less than the money spent on primary school education, and it may even exceed it. But what do we get as a result?" Someone has calculated that the national higher education expenditure has increased from 3.9 million to 33.6 million in twenty years, while the number of students has only increased from 40,000 to 44,000. The waste is conceivable. However, students studying abroad and even university students are not necessarily willing to fulfill their obligations to the country and the nation in primary school education. Those illiterate "illiterates" and primary school students still rely on a few primary school teachers to teach there. Only a group of normal school graduates and secondary school students are responsible for this responsibility. However, students studying abroad return to the country to become officials or university professors, and most of them disdain to engage in this "mass education" cause and disdain to teach "illiterates." The people who advocated running "higher education" first in the past believed that if we run "higher education" and create "specialized talents," we should first develop the domestic industry and commerce. When the country becomes rich, then "primary school education" will naturally become popular. They themselves thought that this was "When the people are numerous, what more is to be added? Enrich them." If the whole country is prosperous, then build more schools so that everyone can enter school and receive education. This is called "When they are enriched, what more is to be added? Teach them." Their view is to have numerous people first, then enrich them, and then teach them after they are rich. However, if we continue to do this, looking at the current poor phenomenon in China, I am afraid that everyone will not even have a school to enter in the future. Everyone knows why China is poor. Our country's poverty is due to the underdeveloped industry and commerce. Then we have to ask where a group of specialized talents who study industry and commerce have gone. One more point, our country's poverty is indeed due to the underdeveloped industry and commerce, but in this era of 20th century production competition, we have not yet learned the ability to "produce," but we have already learned the most fashionable ability to "consume." For example, if others build skyscrapers, we have to live in 20-story洋房, if others take cars, we also have to take cars whenever we go out, even to wearing high hats, wearing formal suits, dancing, and drinking, everyone is "westernized." Who started these things? To be blunt, the first is "students studying abroad" and the second is "university students." We can say that there are definitely no primary school students who would be so "westernized," and definitely no old乡下 who would be so "westernized." So we feel very painful when we talk about it. The poverty of China and the lack of education of the people, part of the responsibility, must be borne by this group of "westernized" scholars. There are many unfair things in the world. Think about where the money for cultivating this group of students studying abroad comes from? Except for some students studying abroad who rely on their ancestors' blessings to have money to go abroad, the rest are always "official expenses." Where does this "official expense" come from? They are all the country's "donations and taxes." Where do the "donations and taxes" come from? They are all the country's "donations and taxes." Where do the "donations and taxes" come from? It is very sad to say, they are all extracted from our people. China has three major donations and taxes: (1) land tax, (2) customs duty, (3) salt tax. These donations and taxes are always added to everyone, regardless of wealth or poverty. In addition, there are "income tax" and "inheritance tax." Foreign countries have long had this method of specifically extracting donations and taxes from wealthy people, but we do not have it in China. I know that there is a rich man in Shanghai who sits at home and has an income of thousands or tens of thousands every day, but I have not heard of the country extracting any "income tax" from him. As for "land tax," it is mostly paid by farmers. "Customs duty" is also mostly paid by farmers. For example, China exports goods, mostly "agricultural products." These "agricultural products" are subject to customs declaration and taxation along the way, and they are all sold as "raw goods" at very cheap prices. Imported goods are always "finished goods." Most of these "finished goods" are daily necessities. Except for a part of "foreign goods" purchased by wealthy families, the rest of the daily necessities are almost sold to various villages in the interior. The donations and taxes on these goods are also added to the general working farmers who purchase them. In addition to the customs duty mentioned earlier, let's look at the "Boxer Indemnity," which was also extracted from customs duties. If we recall why there was the "Boxer Indemnity," it was because the "Boxers" wanted to "support the Qing and destroy the foreigners" that day. Later, they were defeated by the "Eight-Nation Alliance," and the foreigners signed the Treaty of Xin Chou with the Qing court. The foreigners felt that they had to punish China this time, so they asked our country to compensate for their military expenses. However, the indemnity was not calculated based on the number of troops deployed. They calculated it based on the population of China. The indemnity was 450 million Haiguan taels, which is equivalent to fining each Chinese person one tael. Moreover, this indemnity was amortized over 39 years and interest was added. Calculated on the basis of principal and interest, it amounted to 988.223815 million taels, which is equivalent to each Chinese person being fined two taels of Haiguan silver.

Shenbao Radio Weekly

Knowledge of Repairing Heterodyne Radio

— Xiao Mingxiang

Amateur radio researchers may often feel that the principle of heterodyne radios is profound and the structure is complex. Occasionally encountering a broken heterodyne radio, they simply don't know where to start. In fact, the signal frequency (high frequency) amplification, sound frequency amplification, and power supply of heterodyne radios are no different from the commonly seen adjusted high frequency radios. If readers can understand these components completely, then the difficult problems concerning these three components can be solved easily, and this article will not elaborate further.

The reason why heterodyne radios are considered complex is that in addition to the three components, there are also oscillating stages, primary and secondary detection stages, Chinese frequency amplification stages, and various heterodyne reception devices, which cause many difficult problems. This article is limited to explaining the special problems of this heterodyne radio and the repair methods.

Essential Instruments

If a workman wants to do a good job, he must first sharpen his tools. The first essential instrument for repairing heterodyne radios is an electric meter, such as a DC voltmeter, milliammeter, ohmmeter, etc., which are all necessary. However, it is too extravagant to prepare all of them. Fortunately, these electric meters can be used interchangeably. If a radio analyzer (the method of making this device will be described in another article) can be assembled, it will be especially convenient to use.

In addition to the electric meter, the special instrument needed to repair heterodyne radios is an oscillator, which must be able to generate oscillation within the full broadcast band and intermediate frequency band, and its frequency must be absolutely calibrated.

Harmonics

Unless it is a pure sine wave, alternating current often has harmonics higher than its own frequency. When a vacuum tube works in a radio, its characteristic curve can never be a pure straight line. Even the so-called straight line part is slightly curved, so the sine wave is distorted, and many harmonics are often generated.

Harmonics are often multiples of the frequency itself, such as the second harmonic, which is twice the frequency itself, three times three times, four times four times, and so on. The closer the harmonics are to the frequency itself, the stronger the power. For example, the harmonics of the second or third镒, sometimes even the fifth harmonic, can cause interference to the radio. The fourth harmonic of the intermediate frequency of 175KC is 4×175=700KC, that is, the eighth harmonic of this frequency itself is still within the broadcast range. If the radio's isolation device has a slight defect, this harmonic is often easily mixed with the external signal frequency and generates heterodyne action, causing the radio to fail to work legally.

Let's give another example to illustrate. Suppose the radio is tuned to a radio station with a frequency of 690KC. The intermediate frequency stage of the radio is 175KC, then the oscillating stage should be adjusted to 865KC. If the fifth harmonic of the intermediate frequency of 875KC is input into the circuit with the signal frequency for some reason, it will generate a beat frequency of 10000 cycles (Veatfrequency). If the sound frequency stage cannot cut off this frequency, a very sharp strange scream will occur in the loudspeaker. If the intermediate frequency stage is not properly matched, causing the frequency to be slightly lower than 175KC, this symptom will be more likely to occur. Now assume that the intermediate frequency is 174KC. When receiving the same radio station, the oscillating stage frequency must be 864KC. This frequency may be confused with the fifth harmonic of 174KC, which is 870KC, resulting in a beat frequency of 6000 cycles. This frequency is extremely easy to generate a mad scream in the sound frequency stage. Therefore, the intermediate frequency matching problem of heterodyne radios is extremely important, with 175KC being the most suitable. Furthermore, if the oscillating stage frequency and the signal frequency have been accurately matched to be 175KC apart, but the intermediate frequency stage cannot be matched to the same frequency, the radio's sensitivity will be greatly affected, and the effectiveness will be completely lost. (To be continued)

Talking About "Quartz Crystal"

— A Layman

The range of a shortwave transmitter depends not on the size of the power, but on the stability of the oscillation frequency. If it can be adjusted appropriately, a shortwave transmitter with only five or ten watts of power can easily achieve cross-ocean communication. There are many ways to stabilize the frequency, but the most effective is to use a quartz crystal.

An oscillator that uses a quartz crystal to control the oscillation frequency is called a "Crystal Controlled Oscillator." Such an oscillator uses the "Piezo-electric effect" of the quartz crystal to control the oscillation frequency. With this kind of oscillator, the frequency is entirely determined by the size of the crystal: therefore, under normal circumstances, changes in the values ​​in the circuit, heating of the vacuum tube, and fluctuations in the high-voltage power supply should not affect the stability of the frequency. Therefore, this kind of radio communication is not only easy to listen to, but also has a very clear and beautiful tone.

When a quartz crystal is subjected to pressure or tension, an electric field is generated around it. Conversely, when we place it in an electric field, its physical form changes. This effect is called the "piezoelectric effect." Quartz crystals can be used to stabilize oscillation frequency because of this piezoelectric effect. There are actually many things that have a piezoelectric effect. However, quartz is the most suitable, so it is the most widely used.

Naturally occurring quartz crystals are colorless and transparent hexagonal prisms. In Crystallogy, a complete quartz crystal has three "Axes," called X, Y, and Z axes. See the attached diagram for details, where the dotted lines represent the axes. Mined quartz must be cut and polished before it can be used. There are X-cut and Y-cut methods; the details are self-evident in the figure, where the black shadows are the locations of the cut pieces. The X-cut method is also commonly called the vertical cut method, or the Curie cut. The Y-cut method is also called the parallel cut method, or the 30 degree cut.

The X-cut method and the Y-cut method each have their advantages. The Y-cut method is relatively easier to oscillate, but sometimes there are two oscillation frequencies, so the X-cut method is used more often.

The thickness of a fully polished quartz crystal is directly related to the oscillation frequency. According to test results, for the X-cut method, f × t = 112.6; for the Y-cut method, f × t = 77.0; where f is the oscillation frequency in kilohertz, and t is the thickness of the crystal in inches.

The frequency range that such a quartz crystal can achieve is from several kilohertz to fourteen megahertz, but in actual use it is only from forty kilohertz to seven megahertz. Because, as we know from the previous paragraph, the thickness of the quartz crystal is inversely proportional to the oscillation frequency; although theoretically, we can obtain any hypothetical frequency as long as we grind the crystal to an appropriate thickness, the lower frequencies require very large pieces of raw material, which is impossible in fact due to the limitations of natural production; at the same time, crystals with higher frequencies are not suitable because they are extremely thin and easily broken.

During grinding, because quartz is very hard, a grinding agent made of kerosene and fine diamond powder is used for grinding. A well-made quartz crystal is approximately one inch square, its two surfaces should be parallel to each other without unevenness, the surface should be free of oil, and if it is an X-cut, its surface should be perpendicular to the X-axis; for the Y-cut, they should be parallel to each other. Therefore, without appropriate tools and instruments, it is better to buy ready-made products than to grind them yourself. When using it to control oscillation, it should be clamped between two metal plates; there are also crystal holders specially made for this purpose on the market, which are very convenient to purchase.

The quartz crystal in the crystal-controlled oscillator is connected to the grid circuit of the oscillation tube, replacing the variable capacitor and coil in the original grid circuit. Of course, various oscillation circuits can be replaced in this way, but the screen-grid resonant type is the best. Now, let's take a screen-grid resonant crystal-controlled oscillation circuit as an example, as shown in the attached diagram. No more will be said.

To do long-distance communication with low power, using a quartz crystal controlled oscillator is the best there is.

Various Types of Detection (Continued)

— Si Lian

(4) Full-wave detection is the same as half-wave detection, except that the dual-grid does not use parallel full-wave detection. During rectification, its input can be averaged, and it can prevent the carrier frequency from flowing into the triode part, which is its advantage. See Figure 4.

(5) Push-pull detection. Everyone knows that push-pull audio frequency amplification has a very strong amplification power, so using it as push-pull detection can also produce wonderful effects. Figure 5 shows its circuit diagram. R is a four-megaohm resistor, which is used here as a grid leak. After testing the No. 19 vacuum tube, it can indeed reach far. Receiving the Nanjing Central Radio Station is already very loud in the loudspeaker. Selectivity and Sensitivity are excellent, almost equivalent to adding a stage of radio frequency amplification. The author had already tried to install this type of detection last year, but the vacuum tube was not No. 19, but two No. 30 vacuum tubes, and the results were very satisfactory. Now that there are composite vacuum tubes for sale, it should be much more convenient. (End)

International News

Millimeter Wave Communication Shows Promise

"Vatican City," "Papal Palace," and "Centaer Fort" near Rome are experimenting with millimeter-wave communication. The distance between the two places is twenty kilometers. The wavelength used is sixty centimetres (Centimetres), which is twenty-three and a half inches. It is reported that the test results are very good, and research is continuing to seek new developments.

A Powerful Tool for Long-Distance Radio Reception

— Li Yuanqing

——Testing an Antenna Tuner

——Can Increase Output Power by Up to Seven Times——

Although the antenna tuner introduced in this article (Tenatuner) has a very great effect, the internal structure is actually not that mysterious after all. It is just a very simple resonator. When receiving broadcasts from nearby areas, the device can increase the selectivity of the radio. When receiving broadcasts from distant areas, it can increase the output volume and reduce input noise. It is indeed an indispensable tool for general long-distance radio enthusiasts.

The attached diagram shows the wiring method of the device. C1, C2, and C3 are three-gang variable capacitors (the capacitance of each section is .000365 mfd, and after being connected in parallel, it is approximately .001 mfd.). The coil is wound with 150 turns of No. 24 double silk-covered wire on a cylinder with a diameter of three inches and a length of four and a half inches. A tap is taken from each of the 5th, 20th, 50th, and 100th turns—a total of six taps including the beginning and end—and connected to screws 2 to 7. The entire device is installed in an aluminum or copper shielding box. Except for the ground wire terminal, all other parts must be insulated from the metal box.

When using, first connect the wires as shown in the diagram (whether the metal box needs to be grounded must be determined after experimentation; sometimes not grounding the wire can actually improve efficiency). Then, turn the switch SW2 (starting from point 2; point 1 is for the antenna to directly receive the radio). At the same time, adjust the variable capacitor until the radio receives the loudest volume and the clearest sound quality (when adjusting longer wavelengths, if you feel that the capacitance is insufficient, you can turn on the switch SW1).

The simplicity of using this device is as described above, but there is one more thing to pay attention to: when receiving radio stations of any wavelength, it is best to use less inductance and more capacitance. In other words: when resonating, the fewer the number of turns of the coil and the greater the capacitance of the capacitor, the better the results. According to experiments, when the frequency is 600KC, switching SW2 to point 6 can obtain an output power of 7.25. If SW2 is moved to point 7 and the capacitance is increased again, although the circuit can still be resonated, the output power will immediately decrease to 5.3 times—a loss of about one-third.

The following table shows the increase in output power after using the antenna tuner. The table shows the results obtained by American radio experts after using precision instruments for testing. When the frequency is 600KC, the output power is approximately 7.25 times or 17.2 decibels; (please refer to the author's article "The Ratio of Power to Volume" in issue 43 of this journal.) When the frequency is 1500KC, the output power is approximately 1.8 times or 5.1 decibels. The average output power is approximately five times or fourteen decibels.

Comparison of Longwave and Shortwave Communication

— Chong Ling

Shortwave

(1) Shortwave requires simpler transmitting and receiving equipment.

(2) Shortwave antennas are quite short and their structure is also simple.

(3) Shortwave communication can achieve extremely long distances with minimal electrical power.

(4) Shortwave receivers have very sharp resonance, and signals are not easily disturbed by each other.

(5) Atmospheric noise has very little impact on shortwave machines.

(6) But geomagnetic storm disturbances are more pronounced on shortwave.

(7) For shortwave communication, the time and distance of the wave must be properly configured.

(8) Shortwave's ability to reflect off the Heaviside layer is far superior to that of longwave.

(9) Because the ground wave is absorbed and disappears in shortwave communication, and the reflected wave travels far, a skip distance is created, resulting in a silent zone in the middle distance.

(10) Shortwave is prone to the phenomenon of echo signals.

Longwave

(1) Longwave requires more complex transmitting and receiving equipment.

(2) Longwave antennas are very long, and the equipment is also more expensive.

(3) Longwave communication over the same distance requires greater electrical power.

(4) Longwave receivers cannot have sharp resonance, so reception is easily interfered with.

(5) Longwave machines are greatly affected by atmospheric noise.

(6) Longwave is very little affected by geomagnetic storms.

(7) Longwave communication and the distance it can reach are less affected by time.

(8) But longwave propagates along the ground and is not as easily absorbed by the ground as shortwave.

(9) Longwave has no skip distance phenomenon.

(10) Longwave is not like this.

Lack of New Buyers for U.S. Cotton

Yesterday, U.S. cotton opened with a rise or fall of one or two pounds compared to the previous day. The industry closed out bullish March positions and bought forward months. The market price was slightly soft, and investor sentiment was stable. Transactions were mostly for hedging. Liverpool gangs bought March and sold forward months. There were not many new buyers. The industry is waiting for Washington's progress on the new cotton policy and the more obvious development of various businesses. Later, the sell-off by bullish parties and the sale of New Orleans continued to weaken. The close was flat and tired (the 22nd was Washington's birthday and was a holiday). Spot prices did not move, and futures fell by two to three pounds. The British cotton market was weak, with spot prices rising by two points and futures falling by one point. Indian cotton was tired due to the sale of futures merchants and the lack of assistance from buyers, with Pingguoer falling by 0.25 rupees, Aomula falling by half a rupee, and Bailuoxi falling by 1.25 rupees. The original telegram record is on the left (telegram on the 21st).

According to a telegram from Bombay, the opening forecast for Bailuoxi cotton on the 22nd was 246 rupees, up a quarter of a rupee from the previous day's close.

Grain

Forward Flour Covers Shorts, Forward Wheat Cuts Longs

After the flour market opened yesterday morning, the price of foreign wheat rose by about one or two jiao in Chicago, and by eight fen to one jiao or more in Canada. When the prices opened, the market in each month was generally stagnant, and transactions were few. Because this month is close to delivery, floating shorts are covered, and the market sentiment has turned stable. There were few entries and exits in the forward month, and there was no vitality. Until the afternoon opening, because factories covered, investor sentiment turned slightly bullish, and the outside industry slightly transacted in the forward month, and the trend also stabilized. In the future, actual sales will be active, and it can be expected to stand firm, otherwise it will be difficult to be overly bullish. As a result, this month was better by half a fen, April was better by 2.5 li, and the rest were all unchanged.

In the forward wheat market, although foreign wheat was better by one or two jiao or more, at the opening price, this month only had one or two days of trading due to the approaching delivery date. Generally, floating longs were in urgent need of closing out, and due to the silver relationship, there was no intention to recover on the hedging side, so the lowest price was 3 yuan and 7 jiao and 7 fen. The March price also fell to 3 yuan and 8 jiao and 6 fen. Until the afternoon opening, it was still flat at the beginning. Then, the short head slightly covered, returning to one or two fen. However, the combined price of spot foreign wheat is gradually loosening, and the prospect should be less than the hope of being good. As a result, this month was a little less by one fen, March was a little less by three fen, and April was a little less by six fen. The spot wheat market was slightly weak, and the price of medium and inferior goods fell by one or two fen. Delivery was not smooth. The opening price of Shandong Suzhou wheat was 3 yuan and 9 jiao and 2 fen, and the opening price of Bengbu wheat was 3 yuan and 9 jiao. Shen Da sold 400 bales, and Fuxin sold 1,500 bales.

The overseas wheat market stabilized due to rumors of strong winds and dust in the southwestern winter wheat belt. Manufacturers cancelled the May hedging. Due to the large inventories and slow sales of Canadian wheat, some parties doubted the permanence of the pegged price of Canadian wheat.

This situation is still difficult to be considered optimistic for the future of this year's tea market.

Free Talk

Literary Contingency and Necessity

— Zhang Xiangshan

The problem of contingency and necessity in literature is treated in the same way as the problem of contingency and necessity in philosophy. The opinion of critics who obliterate contingency and excessively emphasize necessity has been frequently seen recently. Perhaps because writers excessively utilize contingency to unfold the overall story of their works, critics tend to obliterate contingency.

In old Chinese novels, contingency simply dominates necessity; the two are not linked together. Especially in novels of talented scholars and beautiful ladies, the loss or gifting of a handkerchief or jade pendant often triggers the story's progression. Even in early emerging literature, the depiction of a protagonist's turn or the unfolding of a grand scene relies on a very far-fetched contingency to cascade down. This phenomenon inevitably leaves scars on the work and makes readers feel it is comical and abrupt.

Naturalist writers, who are most faithful to the depiction of facts, do not regard contingent events as natural. Maupassant once said: "When choosing a subject, the artist only selects the necessary and special events from a life full of contingent and worthless events, and removes the contingent events."

"Indeed, many people die in a day due to unexpected disasters, but must artists also depict these unexpected disasters in order to be faithful to the facts? Must they depict the protagonist's head being broken by a falling brick or crushed by a wheel in the middle of the story?"

Indeed, contingency cannot occupy a leading position in creation, because the more contingency there is, the less real it feels; however, the importance of contingency cannot be absolutely denied either.

Originally, in the process of our understanding of reality, necessity and contingency are interconnected and appear on the surface of phenomena. If we absolutely obliterate and deny it because contingency is not easy to blend with reality, then it is too mechanical, that is, too focused on necessity. In fact, the author's skillful handling of these two things can most faithfully express reality. The two are indispensable to each other, and relying solely on necessity is useless. Because the general denial of contingency and the absolute recognition of necessity will inevitably lead to fatalism, that is, belief in an immovable fate. Hegel said: "Due to the general denial of contingency, only simple and direct necessity dominates everything in nature. If we use this kind of necessity as the foundation of philosophy, then we cannot step out of the boundaries of the theological view of nature."

However, how exactly does the writer skillfully handle these two things? In order to explain this problem, let's start with an example to help!

Tolstoy's "Resurrection" not only exposed the judicial system of the Imperial era, but also gave us great lessons, especially in necessity and contingency.

Nekhlyudov seduced Katyusha, a maid in his aunt's house, and had a physical relationship, causing Katyusha to become pregnant and subsequently a prostitute, and was accused of murder. When she was being tried, Nekhlyudov happened to be a juror. As a result, Nekhlyudov began to seek pardon for her, and abandoned his title and distributed his property to track her down to Siberia. The key point of this story is that Nekhlyudov happened to be present in court during the trial. If he had not been present in court, then the story would have had to be interrupted. So this point is a very contingent event. But does this contingent encounter damage the effect of Tolstoy's work? No, because the contingency here is connected to the necessary process in the overall structure.

While tightly grasping the fate of the individual who is typically set, Tolstoy wants to unfold the decisive social problems of the era. By describing the concrete mutual relationships of people living in this situation, and by describing the society they live in with conflicts, he can concretely explain the living connection between contingency and necessity, and the difficult to decompose contradiction. Here, the contingency stopped is a contingent matter, because necessity is revealed in contingency. At the same time, necessity stopped is a necessary matter, because it is due to contingency giving the motive.

Someone once said: "Contingent things have a basis, because they are contingent. But they do not have any basis of the same degree, because they are contingent. Thus, contingent things are necessary, and necessity defines itself as contingency. On the other hand, contingency is also absolute necessity."

Similarly, in literature, when we deal with these two things, first we must analyze historical necessity. We must analyze the protagonist's age, origin, education, and environment, and generally assume their historical mission. Second, we must make this necessity pass through all contingencies and lead to its necessary path. That is to say, the family relies on contingency to develop its necessity, but the important thing is that the basis of necessity must be shown in contingency. Otherwise, it will become an arbitrary arrangement, like a rare treasure falling from the sky. This situation is like the scholar in old Chinese novels encountering difficulties and always being rescued by a chivalrous person, which is generally sudden and rare.

In short, we cannot forcibly separate necessity and contingency; we must connect them with each other. Simply put, it is to "make them seamless." That is, all writers should find necessity in all processes, use necessity as the foundation, make contingency the driving force for developing necessity, and construct the work. I think this will surely rationalize the work and concretely express reality.

Talking About "Essays"

— Tang Tao

It seems that an editor once said: Some articles are difficult to distinguish whether they are novels, essays, or notes, but as long as they have content and are well-written, this situation will still not hinder their greatness.

That's right, this still does not hinder their greatness.

However, if we can distinguish them clearly, thinking that this is an essay, that is a note, and that is a novel, and still not hinder their greatness, that would naturally be even better. But there seem to be not many people doing this kind of "better" work. If there are any, it should start with Mr. Lin Xijun.

Until the recent "Random Notes in Cold Night" in the "Literary Pictorial," Mr. Lin himself does not consider himself "a member of the essayist crowd," but he also writes essays. However, in his essays, one says: "Essays that are hardly considered literary creation"; the principle says: "Trivial and non-genuine literary works of essays"; and three says: "If strictly limited, most of them cannot be accommodated within the realm of literary works. At most, they are just tools used by general essayists to scold people for their own pleasure and have no value."

That's right, essays are tools, and these tools are really powerful. They are taken in Mr. Lin's hands, and he has already scolded himself several times. This time, he simply exiled himself outside the "realm of literary works."

Fortunately, Mr. Lin's "strict limitation" is limited to "most" of them.

But unfortunately, we have no way of knowing how strict Mr. Lin's limitation is. The subject matter of essays is indeed very broad. They also deal with literature, talk about science, discuss society, and satirize politics. If we think that they should be driven out of the "realm of literary works" because of this, then novels, poems, and dramas that draw on society, politics, and science will also be untenable. Only things that specifically describe the lives of literary artists are worthy of being inside the "realm of literary works."

In this way, strict is indeed strict, and Mr. Lin is sitting high in the "realm of literary works," and he is about to sing the "empty city ploy."

If what is limited is the genre, essays are indeed not like novels, poems, and dramas, but they are also not like other papers and narratives in various subjects. This is because they are essays. Since a little can be considered literary works, then most of them are no problem. Because in terms of genre, they are all essays, they are the same.

If it is said to be the style of writing or layout, then there is even less of a problem. The style of writing and layout of essays, like novels, poems, and dramas, vary from person to person. Therefore, there are straight, there are smooth, there are curved, and there are "nonsense."

So what exactly did Mr. Lin see that he expelled essays from the "realm of literary works"? The answer is: This is what he himself said, "completely belongs to a kind of arbitrariness."

If we want to classify essays into or expel them from a certain subject, this is something that requires careful analysis. We really dare not ask him to think calmly about a character like Mr. Lin who has already "lost his soul" when he mentions essays.

Trivial Talks on Historical Vignettes (3)

— Cao Juren

Historical vignettes, in terms of technique, are not much different from humorous vignettes and scientific vignettes. Historical vignettes take materials from historical events, and like humorous vignettes taking materials from humorous stories and scientific vignettes taking materials from natural vignettes, they focus on a certain object. Historical events are so rich that it can be said that it is easy to find subjects; however, the historical events in historical collections are often submerged by the weeds of traditional thought; it is an extremely difficult task to extract the true appearance of history from under the weeds and escape from the vulgar historical view and cultivate the "historical eye" for finding subjects. When we start writing historical vignettes, although we cannot, like general historians, devote all our energy and time to sorting out historical materials, basic work is essential. Discussing history from history, the so-called historical event itself is one thing, and the historical event under the historian's pen is another thing; the historical event itself cannot be repeated or seen again, we can only rely on the historical texts under the historian's pen to speculate on the historical event itself. Here, we must first examine three things; first, examine under what circumstances the historian observed this historical event? Second, examine under what circumstances the historian wrote the historical text? Third, examine under what circumstances this historical text was passed down after it was written? We must have twelve points of patience to trace it back, so that the historical event we grasp is not too far from the true appearance of the historical event. The characters and events of history have been criticized by others using their own moral concepts and power relationships; red faces are loyal ministers, painted faces are treacherous villains, and they are solidified into a stereotyped public opinion. We must have new knowledge of social science and historical philosophy to re-establish the standard of knowing people and discussing the world, so that we can get rid of the ideological constraints of our predecessors, so that we can describe his love of women and rough business character under the stereotype of Guan Yunchang, who is publicly recognized as a saint who does not love beauty or fame and fortune. In the past, those who did historical arguments also had the habit of making revisionist articles. Their observation was not correct, which was similar to the dwarfs watching a drama and discussing it along with the crowd; we must have the magnanimous demeanor of historians, let historical materials guide us to the final conclusion, so that we can avoid the drawbacks of "loving novelty" and "drawing conclusions hastily."

In general, the giants in history, the higher their position, the more they become the target of arrows for ordinary people, and the more they are covered by the added moral coats; artists dare not openly challenge society, and their pens are deterred by traditional sayings, and they dare not have their own original ideas. For example, the chapter on appearance in "A New Account of Tales of the World" records the event of Wen Zhongwu and Yu Wenkang投陶侃. It can be written as a fun drama of literati fearing warriors; however, everyone has the shadow of stories such as Tao Kan moving bricks in their minds, and they definitely dare not write this military閥 (Tao Kan) of the Jingzhou system as a warrior's demeanor, and they definitely dare not intersperse the story of the Jingzhou system military閥 and the Yanghzou system military閥 (Su Jun) competing for power. Another example is that in the late Ming and early Qing dynasties, the storytelling master Liu Jingting was good at elaborating on historical events, and was respected by famous officials and adults at that time for his "ability to directly advise and satirize." However, according to the "Peach Blossom Fan," he said that the paragraph of Confucius' disciple Zhi適齊 in the Analects still does not escape the sour truth of the high-sounding chapters of the Confucian scholars, and it is not seen to be so brilliant, which shows the difficulty of removing traditional ideas. Occasionally I saw a small songbook on the beach, in which the lecture on Confucius going to Ji章 was vivid and interesting, which was a cut above Liu Jingting. I dare to say a sentence now: Those who write historical vignettes should also have the spirit of doubting the ancients and rejecting Confucius first.

The Drunkard

— Chen Fuxi

Tai Laoer swaggered out of the threshold of the Zuileju tavern, humming "Si Lang Visits His Mother." His stomach was full of wine, and he staggered, as if he were about to fall. But just as he was about to go home, he suddenly heard in his ear:

"Laoer, go back quickly, your wife..."

He turned his head to look, and it turned out that the speaker was Pockmarked A-wu.

"Never mind her!"

He shook his head and went his way as usual, thinking in his heart:

"Is my woman really with someone else?"

Every time Tai Laoer had a drink in Zuileju, someone would say this to him, but he never paid attention to it. He always smiled at them and said repeatedly:

"Eh, eh, eh... never mind her!"

After getting drunk, he would go home and sleep; when he woke up, he would have completely forgotten what others had said. Tai Laoer and his wife had always been harmonious, and they even had a son last year. No jokes had ever been made about this son in the Zuileju tavern. One day, the barber Zhang Fu, also full of wine, said with a grin:

"Tai Laoer, is that son really yours?"

"Never mind her!"

"You still don't care even if your wife has a son with someone else?"

"Never mind her."

Tai Laoer continued to drink his wine.

When he was drunk, he did not believe their rumors, but today, he heard Pockmarked A-wu's words again. Although he kept saying "never mind her," he was really unhappy in his stomach. He thought these people were too hateful. Why did they always say these things? Were they joking or was it true?

He staggered along.

"Women, being young, are bound to do things..."

For some reason, he suddenly thought of this, and felt that he was right, so he was angry.

"Damn it! Tell me quickly, are you just hiding it from me?"

"Tell you what!"

"Still pretending to be stupid?"

"You want to die! Why are you acting crazy!"

"Hey, today I will..."

Tai Laoer picked up a teacup and threw it, but he missed, and it shattered on the ground with a "bang."

"I want you to die, you son of a bitch!"

He continued to walk staggeringly, approached her, grabbed her hair and beat her.

His wife cried.

Tai Laoer had vented his anger and ran into the room to sleep. When he woke up, he heard his wife sobbing, and only then did he remember that he had beaten her just now. He thought that his wife was an honest woman who had always treated him well. How could she do such a dirty thing! The words of outsiders were just jokes, how could he have mistakenly beaten his wife in a drunken state. Thinking like this, he really felt extremely uneasy...

The next day, when he went to the Zuileju tavern, he heard others talking about the news of "Tai Laoer beating his wife."

Towards Evening (5)

— Qu Yi

The Da Han Company is a storefront with three large bays and a balcony. On the left and right sides are display windows with very large glass panes. Overdue fabrics are placed messily in the windows. The colors of those fabrics are either excessively green or excessively red; they are all simple original colors, with no mixed colors or overprinting. The patterns on the fabrics are also mostly round flowers or circling dragons. There are absolutely no three-dimensional patterns -- truly preserving the medieval atmosphere of a "rural city." But in front of these fabrics, many flood relief lottery tickets are hung askew: (Each window has a hundred or so tickets hanging.) Proudly fluttering in the evening wind.

A large lampshade hangs over the door of the Da Han Company. The sunlight-like light illuminates a large horizontal strip of gray-black water stains on the cement wall. Like a large iron hoop, it embraces this large foreign-style building around the waist, as if it feared that too many buyers would squeeze into this large foreign-style building and it would explode. But at this moment, besides a few clerks who embellish it like ghosts, there is nothing in the large foreign-style building. Even the sound of talking is silent. It is truly as empty as a grave!

The two people then each exhaled a cold breath. Afterward, a burst of sweat broke out on their bodies.

"Oh! It's hot!" The shorter one turned around, looking directly at the opposite side of the road.

"Yes!" The taller one also turned around, looking to the left and right of the road.

"Isn't this it? Isn't this it?" Suddenly the shorter one shouted, pointing to the one diagonally opposite Xinsheng Road, with a wide green overhanging eave, that storefront. "Isn't it written on this -- on the horizontal strip of this eave, 'Chunyang Inn'?"

"Exactly -- " The taller one was a little unhappy that his companion would actually have this clever discovery. "Exactly -- In Japan, it's not so difficult to find. They don't even install a big electric light on the door platform. It's not at all that. That -- when I was in Japan..."

The two people rushed across the road.

Spring and Autumn

Tidbits

— (Yan Xinquan)

Young writer WW, before he got married, once said to me very seriously: "Women are just a man's plaything." But now that he has married a modern wife, not only can he not treat her as a plaything, but he has become a "slave to the dressing table!"

Old Mrs. Wang is already fifty-one years old this year. Although she has given birth to two sons, she has hardly enjoyed a day of happiness from her sons; once, she said to the neighbors in resentment: "I am just a nanny for them in their infancy, a caregiver in their childhood, now that I am old, in their eyes, I am afraid they regard me as a bulky and superfluous object."

Short Manuscript, Short Talk

— Zhen Lu

This newspaper recently published "New Rules for Submissions," the first of which states: "The shorter the manuscript, the better," opening the chapter and clarifying the meaning, showing people the norm: this is probably a trendy eyebrow style, not hesitating to give it to people with a smile, no need to ask the husband in a low voice, right? Regarding short manuscripts, a discussion can be had.

Civilization advances and human affairs become complicated, and complication leads to simplification, like heat thinking of coolness, which is bound to happen. In the past, when people met, there was usually a series of pleasantries before getting down to business, and it was considered virtuous to elaborate with long talks. Now, they get straight to the point, like a single knife straight in; from this saying of length and short, one can glimpse the trend of world change. Writing uses language to record, and the principle is the same -- readers want to shorten their time by asking for essences, and writers should provide condensed writing. Even the novel, which is most centered on interest, used to be mostly long, but now short ones are also popular, which can be generalized to the rest. Therefore, adapting to the times, short articles have become the beloved of the heavens, which is certainly not accidental.

Fourteen or fifteen years ago, I once created the smallest newspaper, called: "The Smallest Newspaper," and at the same time, Shoujuan wrote the smallest magazine, called: "Purple Orchid Petal," both advocating short poems, which became a trend; essays, novels, and plays were all prefixed with the terms "shortest" or "smallest," like clouds rising and mists steaming. "The youngest boy under the purple orchid mother," leaving a beautiful story in the publishing industry.

I have a novel titled "Universe," the entire piece is a question mark (?); Hu Huaichenjun continued to use the previous title, completing the piece with an exclamation mark (!), this Xu does not write a single word, which can be said to be the shortest manuscript!

Those who praise short poems often say: "Short, small, refined, and valiant," which does not seem quite appropriate; I think: "Refined, sharp, elegant, and eternal," is perhaps closer to the mark. The writing is refined, the reasoning must be sharp, the language is witty and meaningful, and the taste is endless, these four are all possessed, and the ability of short essays and all short manuscripts is complete!

Visiting Plum Blossoms on Lonely Hill

— Ji Chengxing

My foot ailment has just healed, so I invited Mr. Li to visit plum blossoms on Lonely Hill.

Ah, the purity and loveliness of the plum forest, the fragrant aroma that penetrates our hearts, immediately reminds me of the famous line of Lin Chushi: "Sparse shadows slant across the clear water, a faint fragrance floats in the twilight," it is a pity that this is not twilight, if there were a hazy moon, how much more poetic would it be!

Slowly climbing the steps, we rested briefly at the Crane Releasing Pavilion, and then went to visit Lin Chushi's tomb. The plum blossoms here are blooming just right, and there are also many buds waiting to bloom. Because someone is taking care of it, the scenery here is no longer as desolate as it used to be. It is a pity that the plum blossoms have no confidant, and what expression do the tourists have besides superficial praise! Even the poets and celebrities, who would treat them as wives! They only take the unbearably vulgar modern girls here to wander around. If Lin Chushi's heroic soul saw it, I'm afraid he would vomit for three days!

Because my right foot felt sore, after appreciating the plum forest beside the Crane Releasing Pavilion, I had to bid farewell abruptly. Because I was too fond of the plum blossoms, I broke off a branch to take home.

If it were visiting plum blossoms in the snow, how much more fun would it be!

Those Who Are Doomed in the Struggle for Survival

— Tong Fu

Cats and Dogs Infected with the Smoking Habit

— Chen Jingyu

My friend, the owner of Shuangqin Hall, keeps a cat, which is extremely gorgeous, and he cherishes it no differently from an invaluable treasure. The hall owner has a hibiscus habit, and whenever he lies down on a couch, he puts it in his arms and strokes it casually for pleasure. As a result, the cat has become a habit, and as soon as it sees its owner lighting a smoking lamp and bending over to lie down, it jumps onto the bed, squats between its owner's elbows and arms, moves its nose, and smells the thick smoke spewing out, as if it were stereotyped, without a day's or space between. One day, the hall owner was occupied with other matters, and when it was time for the owner to smoke as usual, this cat could not smell the smoke, and the craving broke out. It paced back and forth on the owner's couch, making miserable cries, and yawning repeatedly, with tears and saliva dripping down. The mistress saw it and could not bear it, so she quickly set up the smoking tools and imitated what her husband did, and after a while, it was over.

Recently, a Zhuyou doctor came to our town, carrying two pug dogs, one large and one small; he always takes them with him when he goes to the "smoke selling station" to smoke every day. While he is bending over to burn the smoke, these two dogs are very quiet and curl up beside him, without moving. When he has sucked a mouthful of smoke and drank a mouthful of tea, the larger one immediately goes over and receives the remaining smoke in his mouth, mouth to mouth, and licks his tongue into his mouth, swaying left and right, making a clicking sound. It seems that he does this several times in a row, and then lets the smaller dog do the same work; the large one comes first and then the small one, which is very orderly and has never been argued over. According to the doctor, the smaller dog was originally born to the larger one, and had already contracted a smoking habit in the mother's womb; therefore, since it was born, it has had to be sprayed with smoke several times a day, so that it has become even more addicted than the mother dog.

From this point of view, opium, a kind of thing, not only causes harm to our nation, but also poisons the animal kingdom!

A Glimpse of Ueno Zoo in Japan (Part Two)

— Ji Yun

The pythons of the Malay Peninsula are twenty to thirty feet long, and the Hokkaido bears weigh over a hundred pounds. As for the rest, like pangolins and lizards, there are four or five types of each, with detailed descriptions provided.

The center of the zoo is where the fiercest beasts reside, surrounded by thick iron bars. Inside are three lions and three tigers, as well as leopards and wolves. When a lion roars, all the glass windows in the house rattle, truly befitting the king of beasts. Next to each animal's dwelling is a large open space for them to roam. They frolic in the warm valleys. The long-necked giraffe is a specialty of Africa. Its residence is two stories high, yet still not very comfortable, which demonstrates how long its neck is.

The place of origin is described for each animal. Those found in Japan are mostly collected by themselves. Some are purchased from India, the Malay Peninsula, Australia, and South America. There are not many products from our country, only a very beautiful leopard and the mules commonly seen in Beiping. There are many products from Manchuria and Korea, presumably to show goodwill.

Little Western Paradise

— Written by Zhang Henshui

Chapter Nine: Failing to Flatter and Suffering Rebukes When Seeking Help, Failing to Return Home and Being Misled by Exaggerated Praise

When Yueying heard this, she knew that there was no room for negotiation. What was she waiting for in this room? So, she pouted and said to Madam Hu, "Let's go." Madam Hu could understand very little, but at least understood the words "go" and "scram". She had never worked as a servant for anyone, yet she was being told to scram. There was no need to ask why, as the job was clearly not worth doing. Now that her daughter was helping her up, she also became indignant and excited, and walked out, supporting herself on the door frame. Yueying followed her out of the small courtyard gate, grumbling, "This is my fault. If I had known, I would have gone back earlier. Why did I cry in the yard, feeling scared and cold?" Madam Hu was even more useless than her daughter, having been scolded, and had nothing to say but to raise her sleeves and wipe her tears. By this time, the back door of Little Western Paradise had long been closed, and the mother and daughter groped their way through several layers of rooms, and had no choice but to exit through the main gate. As they walked to the second main building, a large kerosene lamp hung from the roof beam, its flame burning with a whooshing sound, its light as white as silver, so bright that even a fallen needle could be seen. On both sides of the passage were many reclining chairs and tea tables. Tea and cigarettes were placed on the tea tables. Some people reclined in the chairs with their legs crossed, chatting idly. Some people were gathered around a tea table, playing chess. Some people picked up newspapers and read under the lamp. Although not everyone had a smile on their face, no one looked like they were about to cry. When Yueying saw this, she thought to herself, this is something I don't understand. Why are people all eating and dressing, and very happy, while why am I so miserable? She was looking at many people blankly like this when a woman came down the stairs across from them, wearing a light green top and a blue skirt. (140)

Records of Fragrant Imperial Clouds

— Originally by Princess Der Ling of the Qing Dynasty, translated by Qin Shouou

However, what she told us was mostly the same old stories that she had told us before, and we had to pretend to listen with an air of having never heard them before.

"Actors are said to be very devout believers in gods and Buddhas!" Today, she actually told a story that was somewhat new. "Especially towards Guan Gong, who is known as the Demon-Subduing Great Emperor, they are particularly respectful and devout. No matter how cheerful and talkative a person is, as long as it's their turn to play Guan Gong today, they will immediately become solemn. They must first buy a statue of Guan Gong and his horse, carefully fold it, place it high on the table, light incense and candles, and sincerely kowtow. Then they pick it up and carefully tuck it into their own bosom until the play is over. Only then do they take it out, put it back on the table, kowtow again, and finally put it on paper and burn it. Only after going through this whole process can they feel at ease, otherwise they will be uneasy and think that a great disaster is about to befall them."

"Actors are also the most conservative!" The Empress Dowager continued to describe the lives of actors to us. "Every move, every line in the play, the patterns on the costumes, the ornaments they wear, are all regarded as golden rules and laws that must be strictly followed, and they will never change. Not only do they do this for their entire lives, but their descendants and apprentices will continue to do the same!"

These two paragraphs can be said to be extremely pertinent, and I later heard others say the same thing.

I think the literary scenes of old Chinese dramas are still a very beautiful form of opera; as for the martial scenes, they are a bit too lively! Whenever it comes to battles between two armies, the gongs and drums are so loud that they almost deafen people; and the kind of reckless fighting is also too wild, and I don't like to watch it. (251)

Interesting Scientific Facts

Human sense of smell is too poor. If you have ever hunted, when you see a hunting dog moving forward, frantically wagging its nose in the rocks and weeds, can you imagine what it is sensing? I think not only you, but anyone in the world cannot imagine it, simply because the human sense of smell is too poor. Although humans are not weaker than all animals in their sense of smell, compared with the good smellers among mammals, the difference is simply astronomical. If you don't believe it, please look at the interesting experiments recently conducted by Professor Mai Tehai on this issue: A guinea pig (a guinea pig is also one of the mammals with a good sense of smell) has been accustomed to eating barley porridge since childhood. One day, a small amount of arsenic was added to the porridge. It ate it very happily at the time, and as a result, it was poisoned, and for several days it did not dare to approach the barley porridge. Now, in addition to arsenic, it was also given a plate of barley porridge containing nitrified alum (with an almond-like smell) (porridge 50 cm, nitrified alum 80 drops). After a short period of identification, it only ate the latter because the latter had an unusual smell, but it did not have a bad image. After only one day of experience, it had imprinted the fact that only barley porridge with the smell of nitrified alum is "you can eat". From then on, the two types of barley porridge were given at the same time, and the amount of nitrified alum contained in one of them was gradually reduced, from 1:10, 1:100 to 1:10000000. At that time, the guinea pig could still distinguish its smell, and thought it was edible. If it was diluted further, it would no longer be able to feel the existence of nitrified alum, so it hesitated not to eat both. Later, Mr. Mai ordered ten of his top students to do the experiment, giving them as many plates of barley porridge as they did the guinea pig experiment, with the same amount of porridge and nitrified alum, and asked each student to individually record the plate number in which they could still identify the existence of nitrified alum. The result was that they could no longer smell its existence at all when the nitrified alum was diluted to more than 1:100000. From this, it can be seen that the human sense of smell is actually thousands of times worse than that of a guinea pig. That is, a spice that a human can only just feel the aroma of only needs to be one-thousandth of its quantity in a guinea pig, and it can feel the same aroma. What an amazing thing this is!

Scientific Production of Medicine from the Placenta The placenta, or afterbirth, is the membrane that encloses the fetus. The fetus obtains nutrition from the mother and excretes metabolic products through it. Therefore, it is a meritorious servant in the developmental history of every person. However, people who have not received medical knowledge will at least feel uncomfortable when they hear the word "placenta." Even women themselves regard it as an unclean thing. However, almost everything exists. The ancient Chinese medicine, which includes everything, probably recognizes it as a wonderful medicine for calming the mind, nourishing qi, replenishing blood, and benefiting essence (that is, the so-called purple river cart.) Even the "doctor" himself does not know how to calm the mind. (To be continued)

Shen Bao Local Supplement

Talk

Decoration

— Chen San

A piece of lard cake worth three copper coins is placed in a brocade box and displayed in a large glass cabinet. Someone without experience will be stunned and wonder which country this piece of lard cake comes from? Is it a scientifically baked product? Or was a "special technician" hired? The reason is that the decoration is too "luxurious". It makes the piece of lard cake worth three copper coins look "dignified".

A friend who works as a clerk in a cosmetics company told me that the eyes of men and women in the city are born to only pay attention to decoration. When I asked him the reason, he gave me facts to prove it: A lady with her head shrunk in a gray overcoat collar came to buy a bottle of perfume. Even when the best one was given to her, she still shook her head. There was no other way but to put the original product in a Paris glass bottle in the warehouse and double the price. The lady put her nose up to sniff it and praised it as a valuable product. She paid the full price and bought it. In fact, she didn't buy perfume, she bought the Paris glass bottle—decoration.

However, it is not only goods that need decoration to be valuable. In this world where "clothes are valued more than people," people must also pay attention to their "appearance." According to the original meaning of "Buddhas need gold clothes, people need fine clothes," a bamboo cloth robe doesn't seem to make much of an impression. At a banquet, other distinguished guests might mistake you for a servant, and even the host will consider it not very honorable. Moreover, if you want to go up to the seventh floor, the elevator operator will tell you without waiting for you to order: "Run up the escalator yourself!" Oh my god, if you have a beautiful set of clothes on your body, a cigar in your mouth, and a leather bag in your hand... then how comfortable you would be. Pull the iron door, open the iron door, and make people look up to you.

Some honest people will show their honest eyes and accuse this of being "vanity".

However, in this world, "vanity" is somewhat beneficial to life. Lard cake is sold in brocade boxes, so people should pay more attention to their outward "selling point." For example, even if you have not read any foreign languages, you can put a large vacuum tube fountain pen in your pocket. Even if your eyes are not sick, wearing a pair of flat-lens doctorate glasses is enough to add color to your face. Is the world not full of idiots who pursue practicality? Don't think that you can go out and respond to the world just because you have a stomach full of skills. You must first stand in front of the dressing mirror and look at yourself. If you want to make a living in society, I advise you to talk less about practicality. Otherwise, everyone else is eating rice, and you don't even have a bowl of thin porridge to hold.

Or, you will complain again and curse those people who don't know what's good. But how many people in the world really know what's good? In the bathhouse, who doesn't have a naked body? Does Mr. Zhang have any less body parts than Mr. Li? However, one comes out wearing a blue cloth short jacket and trousers, and the other comes out wearing a fur coat. The difference in shape and color is immediately apparent. Of course, this is the difference in "decoration" between the two people. But, you say, which one will people recognize as "upper class"?

Naturally, the one wearing blue cloth short jacket and trousers is the one who was eliminated in the first round. You can't blame people for not knowing what's good, he himself lacks "decoration." It is the same example as the three-copper-coin lard cake that is not packed in a brocade box.

Miscellaneous Notes on Rural Life

— Jia

The most miscellaneous thing is the air that is quiet to the point of being unable to be quieter. This mood, this environment, is most suitable for a person who has long been accustomed to urban life and finally feels disgusted with the noisy atmosphere to take a spiritual rest. Here, there is absolutely no day and night shouting that will cause you to have inexplicable annoyance, which is unique to cities with various vehicles and horses. What there is is a clear blue sky, and the clouds leisurely soaring in the sky above. In addition, there are occasionally one or two train whistles passing from distant villages. But when this sound enters your ears, it has become very soft and long. It will definitely not cause you any discomfort, perhaps it is a rare melody that decorates this too-silent natural world. If you have just slipped out of the high-speed city that is constantly spinning with material machinery, and thrown yourself into the gentle and peaceful embrace of nature, you will deeply feel how vulgar and dark everything in the city is. How refreshing and lively everything in the village is, and at the same time feel as if you have taken off a heavy burden, and there is unspeakable comfort.

The lives of all the people here are healthy and full of energy. Completely unlike the city, where there is no distinction between day and night, and people often sleep until dusk, and they can't see the face of the sun all year round, making everyone's face sickly yellow and gray, without a trace of color. A day's life for the people here is almost equivalent to two days for city people. Their work is more regular: when the sun rises, they begin to work with their hands and feet; when the sun sets, the whole day's work is done, and they rest, have a full stomach, and then each go to find their own fun.

Early in the morning, bathed in the faint morning glow, taking slow steps, walking step by step towards the fields, gentle breezes blowing slowly from the front, closing your lips and taking a deep breath, a new and lively feeling immediately overflows the whole body, and the mind feels unusually relaxed and happy at the same time. And constantly stumbling your feet, with a bit of coolness, are the green grasses containing crystal-like dew, and as you brush past them, they fall to the ground in drops. Maybe there are also small birds singing a morning serenade in the nearby leaves.

Continuing along the way, what you will see is three or five women walking slowly on the ridges, leading children on one side and taking some dirty clothes to the pond to wash on the other side; in the fields far and near, scattered farmers are wriggling and hunching their arms to pull out weeds, and some are pushing ox plows, turning the soil, while scolding the animals and whistling at the same time.

If the spring plowing comes, they will become more busy and cannot be separated. As soon as the sky is bright, they all climb down, take various tools such as hoes and shovels and rush to their own fields. Even the young children who usually just eat white rice and play follow their fathers to help. The whole day is spent in the field. At noon, the housekeepers cook and send meals to them. Sometimes even the housekeepers are busy, so they simply change things like sweet potatoes for rice. They go home only from early morning until the dim sunset in the west. They never think of being lazy, and everyone asks each other.

——Brother Da Mu, your field will soon be plowed, right!

——Rice can be planted in a few days.

Hearing this answer, the questioner will unconsciously feel anxious:

—You have a lot of people, it's really comfortable. Like me, with only one horse, I have to do everything myself. Fortunately, God is good, it hasn't rained for several days. If it rains at this time, wouldn't even the seedlings be unable to be sown? That would be terrible?

The tone is mixed with extreme urgency.

But this seems to be the scenery that exists in my memory. Now that I live in this village again, it is not easy to see the farmers working diligently in the fields as before. Although the tranquility and quietness here are still the same, and the noise and prosperity of the city are also still the same, some things have changed.

Work After Obtaining a Title

— Ding Mo

Uncle

— Li Ni

My mother sent a telegram from home, asking me to quickly pack up and go home, because my uncle's illness was getting worse day by day. According to the doctor, the condition is very serious, and there is probably no hope of recovery. Therefore, we have to prepare to take care of my uncle's funeral affairs, and ask me to go back quickly to help.

It has been a whole six years since I last went to my uncle's house. However, my uncle's life's work and his appearance are still very clearly imprinted in my mind—he is about forty years old, with a medium-sized, thin body, a small head, with a few sparse and messy gray hair, a dark and dry yellowish face, really too thin, without a bit of luster or fullness, simply like a wax figure in a specimen room! His two eyes are deeply sunken like two holes, but the two black pupils are like stars shining in the night sky.

The air in the room was as dead as midnight. At the window, I lowered my head and thought for a while, feeling thousands of melancholy insects squirming in my heart, occupying my whole heart. So, so, I raised my head and looked at the light clouds floating across the blue sky outside the window, light and lonely. At this time, my uncle's house six years ago quickly appeared in my mind.

When my mother was not yet married, my grandfather had died of rheumatism in Nanyang. At that time, my uncle was still young. Because my grandmother only gave birth to my uncle as a son, she would not let my uncle go far away to the "foreign country" to inherit his father's business. At the same time, my uncle was also a gentle and weak scholar who was not used to doing business. It goes without

Page 25

saying that he was an amateur. Therefore, he was happy to enjoy the industry left by his grandfather at home, living a leisurely and elegant life.

I have liked going to my uncle's house since I was a child, because my uncle's study raised many kinds of birds: such as the jumping and singing orioles and thrushes, and even pigeons that can deliver letters, which are the most able to amuse me and make me reluctant to leave.

"Nephew Yun, that gray-winged, hawk-eyed pigeon has laid an egg, so white and big, so cute." Every time I went to my uncle's house, when I met my uncle, he would always tell me with a childlike smile.

"Uncle, just let me raise two little pigeons that look like gray-winged, hawk-eyed." I leaned close to my uncle and squealed, insisting on him promising me, until my uncle nodded.

Time passed like flowing water, without any mercy, and I have not been to my uncle's house for a whole six years. Although I have to return home every year, the shortness of the holidays has made it impossible for me to see my uncle again. But in my mother's letters, I can always learn a little bit about my uncle's situation over the years, knowing about the decline of his family and the desolation of his old age. However, this is just a little bit of my uncle's situation that I have seen in the letters from home.

That day, I took the noon train to leave City T. The next day in the afternoon, my uncle's house appeared before my eyes. The tall white powder walls were not as white as they were six years ago, and they were peeling off in patches. The black lacquered gate had also faded, and the bright golden bronze door knocker was covered with a thick layer of green rust, showing a kind of decadent and down-and-out atmosphere under the slanting sunlight.

When I pushed open the two faded and peeling doors, the green lilac flowers with graceful and charming姿态 that had supported her with a wooden frame stood lonely. Orioles, thrushes, and pigeons, not even a feather was left. Everything was deserted and unexpectedly showed an atmosphere of decline. After walking through the deserted gate lane and entering the central hall, the air suddenly became solemn. My mother and aunt were surrounding my uncle's thin body, crying sadly.

In addition, everything was silent, showing an atmosphere of decline.

Sickness

— Dai Ni

They took shelter from the drizzle and slanting wind in a single-front cafe.

When she sat down opposite him, rubbing her hands, the plump, watermelon-like White Russian woman bowed to the patrons with an ugly smile. Without asking for her consent, he ordered two glasses of sweet wine and a plate of milk cake.

It was three o'clock, the quietest time in the cafe. The owner of the shop turned to the back of the counter, and the two unexpected guests sat in the warm-as-spring elegant room.

"I received her letter yesterday morning saying that she had spent two months of married life in the sanatorium. That's funny enough! Escaping from the thermometer and the confinement room of the white-clad girls, watching movies every day for entertainment, hoping that I would come to Cathay today at three o'clock to be her companion."

He wanted to meet her in the wind and rain, but she said she didn't like to watch the movie starring Butterfly Madame, so she came here to take shelter from the rain for no reason.

She looked in the mirror and arranged her hair that was messed up by the wind, saying as if to herself: "I've really gained weight lately!"

"I also want to go to the sanatorium, I'm too thin!"

I didn't want such a casual remark to cause her dissatisfaction. Do you think it's okay to do that? "A living person being a prisoner of the thermometer!"

The shop owner respectfully delivered the food and retreated to the back of the counter. From her smile when she left, I felt that she was fantasizing about a sweet dream.

"That guy is thinking about being a duchess!"

"You've really changed! Don't you have any sympathy for a weak woman stranded in a foreign country!"

She raised her glass, put it down without touching a drop of green liquid, and looked all over him with her eyes, making him afraid to look at her, as if she was going to do a deed of heroism admired by thousands of people today.

"Two months seem to have passed for three years..." She shook her head and swallowed the meaning underneath along with the wine.

He couldn't answer any more. In fact, there was nothing to say. Looking at the rows of foreign wine bottles in the cabinet, he suddenly thought that if that fat guy straightened his back and stood in front, he couldn't help but laugh.

"It's really worth your laugh, spending your honeymoon in the sanatorium!"

As if after the rain, everything was exposed from the dark clouds. Women are so thoughtful and far-sighted. "Miss, you misunderstood my meaning. Do you think I can still bring a bouquet of flowers to your bedside every day to greet you? You also have to have some sympathy for a hero who has returned defeated from the battlefield!" He angrily finished the wine in front of him.

"Hmph! That rogue! He sent me to the hospital but ran away! Don't you know?"

He almost wanted to laugh again.

"Yes, the newspaper told me that he failed to make a fortune; but in another occasion, he did not declare failure!"

She showed a sincere smile, this smile evoked the emotions he had long forgotten. He felt himself gradually great. If he stood in front of the foreign wine bottle cabinet, he could win victory from the duchess. To celebrate her completion of the work of heroism, he raised his glass, but it was an empty glass.

The moment he left the cafe, the people who had just left the three o'clock movie came in. The sky stopped raining, and the slanting wind brushed against his face, and he felt a slight breath of spring. Walking past the gate of Cathay again, he looked at the advertisement picture of Shirby Schneidemei and said to her:

"Are you going to the US Consulate to ask when the cherry blossoms will bloom again?"

"How annoying! I don't like watching her movies!"

Yao Xiao'an Wang Pingqiu Qilin Leopard

China and the West (1040) 11:00 PM to 12:00 AM

Opening (Social Skills)
