Shen Bao This Area Supplement Film Special

"David Copperfield" Made into a Film

— Xiying

Detailed Research Striving for Perfection

Characters in the Play Fit the Original Scenery

Dickens' famous novel, "David Copperfield," has now been brought to the screen. When the film is released in Shanghai in the future, we can see the scenery and characters of Dickens' era in the eighteenth century, because the production of "David Copperfield" is meticulously researched, even in the smallest details, and there are no flaws to be found. Those who have read Dickens' original book or Lin Qinnan's translation must have an image of all the characters in the book in their minds, their appearance, speech, and actions. After they see "David Copperfield" on the screen, they will definitely clap their hands and applaud, because the appearance, speech, and actions of all the characters on the screen can be said to coincide with what they imagined in their minds.

Let us temporarily put aside the configuration of all the characters in the play and first talk about the preparations for the filming of this film.

About a year and a half ago, David Selznick, the young producer who created the amazing success of "Little Women," began to look for material that could be compared to "Little Women." At that time, the director of "Little Women," George Cukor, also sympathized with him. There was also a writer, Howard Estabrook, the author of "Cimarron," who was also very enthusiastic. So the three of them joined forces and sought out excellent material together.

The subsequent events cannot be described in detail here. In short, in November 1933, after they had decided to adopt Dickens' "David Copperfield," in order to make the atmosphere in the film realistic, they found several first editions of Dickens' novels, because in those books, there were portraits of characters hand-painted by the artist Phiz of Dickens' era. They used those portraits as blueprints for filming, because those portraits had been personally selected by Dickens himself, who believed that they were exactly like the people in his book. In addition, there were also pen drawings by Hablot Knight Browne, which were adopted after Phiz's suicide, and were also used as a reference. These drawings were reprinted many times as reference materials for the authorities. This is why the characters on the screen coincide with what readers of Dickens' novels imagine in their minds.

The meticulous research of their staff is not limited to the appearance of the characters. They also sent photographers to London to photograph everything related to the eighteenth century, regardless of size. As a result, they took as many as 70,000 photos, including the style of the eighteenth-century stocks, as well as the wallpaper on the walls, locks and keys, fabrics, etc. It was truly all-encompassing and meticulous. These many photos were shipped back to the United States and became the basis for the MGM scenery department to arrange the furnishings and utensils.

In London, they also found a tailor shop that specializes in making eighteenth-century clothing for stage performances. They found this tailor shop and received a lot of help, because that tailor shop also had a history of everything. They had paintings and photographs of various eighteenth-century clothing. They found this tailor shop and commissioned them to make clothes and accessories for all the roles in "David Copperfield." In this way, the style of the clothes in "David Copperfield" can be said to be very well-founded.

In June 1934, Cukor, Estabrook, and Selznick felt that this was not enough and that they had to go and inspect it themselves. So they went to London together to collect customs and customs. They first started from Blunderstone, the birthplace of David Copperfield (the protagonist of the book), and examined it, and then went through Yarmouth, Dover, Canterbury, and other places according to the program in the book. They also met Mr. Hugh Walpole, the vice president of the British Dickens Society, and asked him to help, and persuaded him to go to Hollywood to join the production work and serve as a screenwriter. Walpole also readily agreed and served as the supervisor of the production of "David Copperfield."

The writing of the script was a very difficult task. They wrote it eight times in total, because Dickens' original book was very long, and it was quite a difficult task to shorten it into a film. There were eight people engaged in writing, with Walpole as the main brain, but they all felt helpless from time to time. For example, there were a total of thirty-seven banquets described in Dickens' original book, which one should be used now?

Then, talking about the characters in the play, the film script only used twenty-six important roles, but there were more than three times as many characters in the original book that could be called important. In addition to the important roles, there were at least fifty minor roles that spoke, and it was necessary to find appropriate people. The various difficulties and anecdotes were even more numerous. For example, Chauncey Olcott was chosen to play Micawber in the book. Because Micawber was bald, he shaved his head completely. When he went to the set the next day, the director felt that he didn't look like the poor Micawber, so he replaced him with someone else. He shaved his head for nothing and became a monk.

Film Reviews

Review of "Mr. Wang's Secret"

— Ling He

— Golden City Screening —

Some people say, "Don't make people cry anymore, Chinese movies need comedies." But movies are not like last year was "Women's National Goods Year" and this year is "Students' National Goods Year," which are so clearly distinguished.

But at this time we saw "Mr. Wang's Secret" after "Mr. Wang." The story of "Mr. Wang's Secret" seems to be more complete than "Mr. Wang." At least there is a story here that is quite connected from beginning to end. If we don't have higher hopes at all, then this story expresses to some extent the universal life and ideas of the petty bourgeoisie. Mr. Wang and Little Chen are indeed a certain type of character in the current city. They represent the vulgar psychology of ordinary citizens. Their philosophy of "there are three unfilial acts, and having no offspring is the greatest," at the same time, in addition to the wife, they are also very interested in taking concubines. Naturally, this reflects the ugly phenomena of advertising for marriage or calling for help to commit suicide. The playwright happily shouted out the slogan of overthrowing men who insult women, and the dancer's way of life of committing suicide is also satirized by the playwright. However, the dancer's way of life of committing suicide is precisely the tragedy of society. The author with a sense of justice should expose the social pathology from the front, and not just finish it with a satire. To put it more deeply, the entire story has no deep meaning, but it is just a superficial exaggeration of social phenomena, without any essential review, and the degree of exaggeration is almost unreasonable.

Speaking of this aspect, we believe that slapstick movies are by no means unreasonable messing around. Hollywood slapstick films have given us ample proof that that kind of idiotic laughter has little artistic value other than making people laugh. In other words, if slapstick films continue like this forever, it will be inevitable to decline. Reality should also be truly reflected in comedies, and slapstick films should also be the expression of film art. Therefore, writers who are loyal to film art must undoubtedly first strive for artistic gains.

"Mr. Wang's Secret" still inevitably contains some shortcomings in terms of performance techniques. The purpose of the playwright or director is to make people laugh, but as a result, because of excessive exaggeration, such as Mr. Wang and Little Chen catching chickens, such as washing clothes, etc., the effect of laughter is destroyed by repeated repetition and unreasonable exaggeration. As for the dancer's suicide, there is also an error in the weaving method, committing the problem of not being able to connect.

Some people say that the advantage of this film is that it does not make people laugh with actions, but the story is funny. Indeed, there is no very rigid slapstick, but the exaggeration of actions is the reason why the work is not successful. All in all, this work is more commendable in Chinese slapstick films, that is, it is not completely messing around with the so-called slapstick face.

Review of "Evergreen"

— Hualun

"Evergreen" — Cathay Screening

This film begins with a brief narrative of twenty-five years ago as a prelude, writing about the famous name of a song and dance queen, Hallie Green, and the tragedy of her unfortunate marriage. The director's handling of the heroine's glory in success, and the quiet departure of self-sacrifice in the burning of love, are quite successful in terms of psychological expression and the setting of the atmosphere of the drama.

The unfolding of the whole drama is today, twenty-five years later, and the plot is discovered from an unknown young actress, Hallie Hawks. After she was rejected many times for the opportunity to perform in a drama group, she was met by a countess, saying that her appearance was very similar to the red-lipped Hallie Green of the past, and after inquiring about her life in detail, she was introduced to the theater owner as Green's daughter, and at the same time, through a publicist, Tommy, who was suffering from his own anonymity, he promoted her in the newspaper, saying that someone who had disappeared had come back again. So, as the news spread, Hawks learned her mother's song and dance style, put on makeup and performed, and won great success. At the same time, she was also noticed by her mother's lover, Marquis Staines, and her original father, and things started to become entangled from then on.

Naturally, like all films, without exception, there are love scenes, and the protagonists of love at this time are naturally Hallie Hawks and the young publicist, Tommy.

At this time, her father, using the same means as he had used to blackmail her mother in the past, repeatedly blackmailed this young couple. She hated it so much that she exposed this fake incident in one of the performances. So, in the uproar of the audience, and in the trial of the court, the lovers became married.

In such a story, under the appropriate handling of the screenwriter, such as emphasizing the misfortune suffered by the mother and daughter, making a deep criticism and exposure of the men, especially the men who are husbands and fathers, the theater operators, publicists, etc., who do not hesitate to deceive the audience in order to make money and become famous, as well as the audience's worship. Then, the success of this script will naturally not be limited to the ordinary song and dance films like the present.

Judging from the current performance, the success of the screenwriter is far less than that of the director. For example, the events of twenty-five years ago cannot be technically inserted into the progress of the drama, but are cut off and placed at the beginning of the film. The countess's meeting with Hawks in the coincidence of Tommy calling her to wait for the opportunity is also not technical enough.

Director Victor Saville has quite commendable things, such as drinking high heels as champagne glasses, and striking glasses with knives and forks to make a sound, etc., which are satirical of aristocratic gentlemen. The use of cigars in several places shows intelligence. The use of lenses and the weaving of pictures are also quite lively and lively, such as starting to write Green on the successful stage "cut off" to the banquet, Tommy's insertion of cigars in the theater director Ben's mouth "cut off" to his training members with smoke in his mouth. When Green left, she looked at the stage lights of her farewell performance being extinguished one by one in the car, etc., which were clean and profound. The expressions and descriptions of the youthfulness of the two young people, Tommy and Hawks, when they stayed together are also more commendable than those from the comedians.

Among the actors, I think Betty Balfour, who plays the director of the drama group, Ben, is the best. Of course, the key scenes of Kitty McKintosh's Hallie Hawks and Sonny Hale's Tommy cannot be underestimated either.

Notice to Those Who Seek the Lyrics of Joyful Forest

After the news that Joyful Forest Company was distributing the lyrics of "Remnant Flower Song" and "New Family" interspersed in "Three Daughters-in-Law" came out, hundreds of letters requesting the lyrics piled up every day. All of them have now been sent out, but with this large number of letters, it is inevitable that there will be a small number of letters that are lost or have the address written incorrectly and cannot be sent to those who request them. Now, in order to make up for this shortcoming, please pay attention to those who seek the song lyrics. If you have not received the song lyrics one week after sending the request letter, please send a letter stating the date of dispatch, mailing address, and name to the Joyful Forest Publicity Department. After checking, it will be resent.

Film Novel

National Voice (Bordertown) (8)

— Xue Mei

Mary Rooke indeed reported Johnny Ramirez, saying he was the murderer who forced her to kill her husband. On the day of the trial, it alarmed all parts of the border, and even the Los Angeles newspapers prominently published Johnny Ramirez's name, because by this time, Johnny Ramirez's name was known to many people. Dale Elwell was also one of the social figures who knew Johnny. Johnny had even written a letter to her.

Johnny Ramirez was locked in jail. The jailer came to tell him that someone had come to visit him. Johnny thought it was Dale Elwell, so he jumped up and asked, "A woman—young—very beautiful?" The jailer scolded, "I don't know, go see for yourself." Johnny had no choice but to follow him and walk out of the iron gate. Outside, a woman called his nickname, "Juanito." Indeed, it was a woman, but neither young nor beautiful. It was his mother. She was wearing a large shawl common to Mexican women. The Persian lamb coat, although Johnny had bought it for her long ago, she still couldn't get used to wearing it. Accompanying her was the priest from Sonora. Johnny never thought that his mother was still alive and would come to visit him. His mother hugged him and tremblingly asked, "You didn't commit that crime, did you?" Johnny said, "Mom, I didn't."

In the courtroom, Johnny's mother and the priest sat with him. Johnny looked around, but he couldn't see his sweetheart. After a while, the prosecutor stood up and said, "I request the presiding judge to call the first witness—Mary Rooke." A female prison guard led Mary Rooke in. She was casually dressed, without any makeup. She walked into the witness stand and took the oath. The prosecutor began to question her, "How long had you known the defendant before your husband died?" Mary replied, "Eight months." The prosecutor then asked, "Where did you first meet him?" Mary seemed not to have heard the prosecutor's words. Her eyes stared straight at Johnny. The prosecutor asked again, "I ask you, Mrs. Rooke, where did you first meet the defendant?" She still didn't hear. The whole court was silent, waiting for her answer, but she still stared at Johnny without speaking.

The judge looked at Mary Rooke, finding her expression strange and somewhat suspicious, so he instructed again, "Please answer the question you were asked." Mary seemed to have heard something. She seemed to have struggled to move her eyes away from Johnny. She began to laugh. At first, she laughed softly, then louder and louder, until she was yelling and screaming wildly. In her wild screams, there were also many intermittent sentences, fragmented words: "He's young... he should be alive... fat and big... he's still so fat... I saw it... Johnny told me to look at him... he already told Sam... when I sleep at night..." It was clear that Mary Rooke was insane. The first witness was impossible to examine, and the case could not proceed.

After the case was dismissed, Johnny Ramirez got into his car, crossed a stretch of desert, and arrived in Los Angeles. It was late, but there was still time to see Dale Elwell and tell her of his love. He arrived at the Elwell's house, and the doorman seemed to know his purpose, coldly saying, "Miss Elwell is about to go out." Johnny said, "Oh, she's going out, I'm coming in. Go tell her." As he spoke, he strode in.

At this moment, Dale Elwell was wearing an evening dress, with a coat draped over her shoulders, walking down the stairs. Seeing Johnny come in, she greeted him and said, "Johnny, you're here. Did they give you trouble?" Johnny laughed, "No, no. What bothered me the most was not being able to keep the appointment that day." Dale said, "I also thought about going to court that day, maybe I could give you some spiritual help. But, you know, my family would definitely not allow me to go. What could I do?"

What Dale Elwell said was perhaps not as affectionate as Johnny had expected, but he didn't blame her too much. He said, "Okay, let's go out together—let's go out to eat." Dale said, "Oh, Johnny, I'm so sorry. When you came, I was just about to go out. I'm already half an hour late. I have to go to a formal banquet—you know, at the house of one of our longtime family friends." Johnny said, "That doesn't matter. I'll take you there." (To be continued)
